margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/16px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/24px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 2x" width="16"/>&#160;&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>\n</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>\n</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Budget  </div></th><td><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">&#8364;</a>5.72 billion <br/>(~<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>6.6 billion) (2019)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budget2019_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-budget2019-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.6em;">Website</th><td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="https://www.esa.int/" rel="nofollow">www<wbr/>.esa<wbr/>.int</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>European Space Agency</b> (<b>ESA</b>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Agence spatiale europ&#233;enne</i>, <b>ASE</b>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Space_Agency_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Space_Agency-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Europ&#228;ische Weltraumorganisation</i>) is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organisation" title="Intergovernmental organisation">intergovernmental organisation</a> of 22 member states<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-members-6">[6]</a></sup> dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">exploration of space</a>. Established in 1975 and headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, France, ESA has a worldwide staff of about 2,200 in 2018<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and an annual budget of about &#8364;5.72 billion (~US$6.6 billion) in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budget2019_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-budget2019-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p><p>ESA\'s space flight programme includes <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">human spaceflight</a> (mainly through participation in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> program); the launch and operation of unmanned exploration missions to other planets and the Moon; Earth observation, science and telecommunication; designing launch vehicles; and maintaining a major <a href="/wiki/Spaceport" title="Spaceport">spaceport</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">Guiana Space Centre</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kourou" title="Kourou">Kourou</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>. The main European launch vehicle <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a> is operated through <a href="/wiki/Arianespace" title="Arianespace">Arianespace</a> with ESA sharing in the costs of launching and further developing this launch vehicle. The agency is also working with NASA to manufacture the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_Spacecraft" title="Orion Spacecraft">Orion Spacecraft</a> service module, that will fly on the <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">Space Launch System</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The agency\'s facilities are distributed among the following centres:\n</p>\n<ul><li>ESA science missions are based at <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Research_and_Technology_Centre" title="European Space Research and Technology Centre">ESTEC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Noordwijk" title="Noordwijk">Noordwijk</a>, Netherlands;</li>\n<li>Earth Observation missions at <a href="/wiki/ESA_Centre_for_Earth_Observation" title="ESA Centre for Earth Observation">ESA Centre for Earth Observation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Frascati" title="Frascati">Frascati</a>, Italy;</li>\n<li>ESA Mission Control (<a href="/wiki/European_Space_Operations_Centre" title="European Space Operations Centre">ESOC</a>) is in <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a>, Germany;</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/European_Astronaut_Centre" title="European Astronaut Centre">European Astronaut Centre</a> (EAC) that trains astronauts for future missions is situated in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, Germany;</li>\n<li>a research institute created in 2009, the <a href="/wiki/European_Centre_for_Space_Applications_and_Telecommunications" title="European Centre for Space Applications and Telecommunications">European Centre for Space Applications and Telecommunications</a> (ECSAT), is at <a href="/wiki/Harwell_Science_and_Innovation_Campus" title="Harwell Science and Innovation Campus">Harwell</a>, England;</li>\n<li>and the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Astronomy_Centre" title="European Space Astronomy Centre">European Space Astronomy Centre</a> (ESAC) is located in <a href="/wiki/Villanueva_de_la_Ca%C3%B1ada" title="Villanueva de la Ca&#241;ada">Villanueva de la Ca&#241;ada</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comunidad_de_Madrid" title="Comunidad de Madrid">Madrid</a>, Spain.</li></ul>\n<div links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESRO" title="ESRO">ESRO</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ELDO" title="ELDO">ELDO</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ESA-ESTEC5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/ESA-ESTEC5.jpg/220px-ESA-ESTEC5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/ESA-ESTEC5.jpg/330px-ESA-ESTEC5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/ESA-ESTEC5.jpg/440px-ESA-ESTEC5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ESA-ESTEC5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Space_Research_and_Technology_Centre" title="European Space Research and Technology Centre">ESTEC</a> buildings in <a href="/wiki/Noordwijk" title="Noordwijk">Noordwijk</a>, Netherlands. ESTEC was the main technical centre of ESRO and remains so for the successor organisation, ESA.</div></div></div>\n<p>After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, many European scientists left <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> in order to work with the United States. Although the 1950s boom made it possible for Western European countries to invest in research and specifically in space-related activities, Western European scientists realised solely national projects would not be able to compete with the two main superpowers. In 1958, only months after the <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_crisis" title="Sputnik crisis">Sputnik shock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edoardo_Amaldi" title="Edoardo Amaldi">Edoardo Amaldi</a> (Italy) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pierre_Auger" title="Pierre Auger">Pierre Auger</a> (France), two prominent members of the Western European scientific community, met to discuss the foundation of a common Western European space agency. The meeting was attended by scientific representatives from eight countries, including <a href="/wiki/Harrie_Massey" title="Harrie Massey">Harrie Massey</a> (United Kingdom).\n</p><p>The Western European nations decided to have two agencies: one concerned with developing a launch system, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Launcher_Development_Organization" title="European Launcher Development Organization">ELDO</a> (European Launch Development Organization), and the other the precursor of the European Space Agency, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESRO" title="ESRO">ESRO</a> (European Space Research Organisation). The latter was established on 20 March 1964 by an agreement signed on 14 June 1962. From 1968 to 1972, ESRO launched seven research satellites.\n</p><p>ESA in its current form was founded with the ESA Convention in 1975, when ESRO was merged with ELDO. ESA had ten founding member states: Belgium, Denmark, France, West Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland, and the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> These signed the ESA Convention in 1975 and deposited the instruments of ratification by 1980, when the convention came into force. During this interval the agency functioned in a <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> fashion. ESA launched its first major scientific mission in 1975, <a href="/wiki/Cos-B" title="Cos-B">Cos-B</a>, a space probe monitoring <a href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_astronomy" title="Gamma-ray astronomy">gamma-ray emissions</a> in the universe, which was first worked on by ESRO.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_activities">Later activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3471" data-file-width="2311" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg/170px-Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg/255px-Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg/340px-Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ariane_1_Le_Bourget_FRA_001.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mock-up of the <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Ariane_1" title="Ariane 1">Ariane 1</a></span></div></div></div>\n<p>The ESA collaborated with <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> on the <a href="/wiki/International_Ultraviolet_Explorer" title="International Ultraviolet Explorer">International Ultraviolet Explorer</a> (IUE), the world\'s first high-orbit telescope, which was launched in 1978 and operated successfully for 18 years. A number of successful Earth-orbit projects followed, and in 1986 ESA began <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giotto_mission" title="Giotto mission">Giotto</a>, its first deep-space mission, to study the comets <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comet_Halley" title="Comet Halley">Halley</a> and <a href="/wiki/26P/Grigg%E2%80%93Skjellerup" title="26P/Grigg&#8211;Skjellerup">Grigg&#8211;Skjellerup</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hipparcos" title="Hipparcos">Hipparcos</a>, a star-mapping mission, was launched in 1989 and in the 1990s <a href="/wiki/Solar_and_Heliospheric_Observatory" title="Solar and Heliospheric Observatory">SOHO</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulysses_probe" title="Ulysses probe">Ulysses</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> were all jointly carried out with NASA. Later scientific missions in cooperation with NASA include the <a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini&#8211;Huygens">Cassini&#8211;Huygens</a> space probe, to which ESA contributed by building the <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a> landing module <a href="/wiki/Huygens_(spacecraft)" title="Huygens (spacecraft)">Huygens</a>.\n</p><p>As the successor of <a href="/wiki/European_Launcher_Development_Organisation" title="European Launcher Development Organisation">ELDO</a>, ESA has also constructed rockets for scientific and commercial payloads. <a href="/wiki/Ariane_1" title="Ariane 1">Ariane 1</a>, launched in 1979, carried mostly commercial payloads into orbit from 1984 onward. The next two versions of the Ariane rocket were intermediate stages in the development of a more advanced launch system, the <a href="/wiki/Ariane_4" title="Ariane 4">Ariane 4</a>, which operated between 1988 and 2003 and established ESA as the world leader<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in commercial space launches in the 1990s. Although the succeeding <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a> experienced a failure on its first flight, it has since firmly established itself within the heavily competitive commercial space launch market with 82 successful launches until 2018. The successor launch vehicle of <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ariane_6" title="Ariane 6">Ariane 6</a>, is under development and is envisioned to enter service in the 2020s.\n</p><p>The beginning of the new millennium saw ESA become, along with agencies like NASA, <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">JAXA</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISRO" title="ISRO">ISRO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">CSA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">Roscosmos</a>, one of the major participants in scientific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_science" title="Space science">space research</a>. Although ESA had relied on co-operation with NASA in previous decades, especially the 1990s, changed circumstances (such as tough legal restrictions on information sharing by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" title="Military of the United States">United States military</a>) led to decisions to rely more on itself and on co-operation with Russia. A 2011 press issue thus stated:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-international-coop_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-international-coop-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Russia is ESA\'s first partner in its efforts to ensure long-term access to space. There is a framework agreement between ESA and the government of the Russian Federation on cooperation and partnership in the exploration and use of outer space for peaceful purposes, and cooperation is already underway in two different areas of launcher activity that will bring benefits to both partners.\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Notable outcomes are ESA\'s include <a href="/wiki/SMART-1" title="SMART-1">SMART-1</a>, a probe testing cutting-edge new space propulsion technology, the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Express" title="Mars Express">Mars Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venus_Express" title="Venus Express">Venus Express</a> missions, as well as the development of the Ariane 5 rocket and its role in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a> partnership. ESA maintains its scientific and research projects mainly for astronomy-space missions such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corot_(space_mission)" title="Corot (space mission)">Corot</a>, launched on 27 December 2006, a milestone in the search for <a href="/wiki/Exoplanet" title="Exoplanet">exoplanets</a>.\n</p><p>On 21 January 2019, <a href="/wiki/ArianeGroup" title="ArianeGroup">ArianeGroup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arianespace" title="Arianespace">Arianespace</a> announced a one-year contract with the ESA to study and prepare for a mission to mine the moon for lunar <a href="/wiki/Regolith" title="Regolith">regolith</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission">Mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The treaty establishing the European Space Agency reads:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treaty_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-treaty-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>ESA\'s purpose shall be to provide for, and to promote, for exclusively peaceful purposes, cooperation among the European States in space research and technology and their space applications, with a view to their being used for scientific purposes and for operational space applications systems\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>ESA is responsible for setting a unified space and related industrial policy, recommending space objectives to the member states, and integrating national programs like satellite development, into the European program as much as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-treaty_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-treaty-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dordain" title="Jean-Jacques Dordain">Jean-Jacques Dordain</a> &#8211; ESA\'s Director General (2003-2015) &#8211; outlined the European Space Agency\'s mission in a 2003 interview:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Today space activities have pursued the benefit of citizens, and citizens are asking for a better quality of life on Earth. They want greater security and economic wealth, but they also want to pursue their dreams, to increase their knowledge, and they want younger people to be attracted to the pursuit of science and technology.\n</p><p>I think that space can do all of this: it can produce a higher quality of life, better security, more economic wealth, and also fulfill our citizens\' dreams and thirst for knowledge, and attract the young generation. This is the reason space exploration is an integral part of overall space activities. It has always been so, and it will be even more important in the future.\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities_and_programmes">Activities and programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Activities and programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Space_Agency_programs_and_missions" title="List of European Space Agency programs and missions">List of European Space Agency programs and missions</a></div>\n<p>ESA describes its work in two overlapping ways: \n</p>\n<ul><li>For the general public, the various fields of work are described as <b>Activities</b>.</li>\n<li>Budgets are organized as <b>Programmes</b> <i>(British spelling retained because it is a term of official documents).</i> These are either Mandatory or Optional.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the ESA website, the activities are:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Observing the Earth</li>\n<li>Human Spaceflight</li>\n<li>Launchers</li>\n<li>Navigation</li>\n<li>Space Science</li>\n<li>Space Engineering &amp; Technology</li>\n<li>Operations</li>\n<li>Telecommunications &amp; Integrated Applications</li>\n<li>Preparing for the Future</li>\n<li>Space for Climate</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Programmes">Programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horizon_2000" title="Horizon 2000">Horizon 2000</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cosmic_Vision" title="Cosmic Vision">Cosmic Vision</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Living_Planet_Programme" title="Living Planet Programme">Living Planet Programme</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Copernicus_Programme" title="Copernicus Programme">Copernicus Programme</a> <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.esa.int/Our_Activities/Observing_the_Earth/Copernicus" rel="nofollow">[1]</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/ExoMars" title="ExoMars">ExoMars</a> <a class="external autonumber" href="http://exploration.esa.int/mars/46048-programme-overview/" rel="nofollow">[2]</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a> <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.esa.int/Our_Activities/Navigation/Galileo/What_is_Galileo" rel="nofollow">[3]</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/FAST20XX" title="FAST20XX">FAST20XX</a></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mandatory">Mandatory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mandatory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Every member country must contribute to these programmes, listed according to:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Technology Research Programme</li>\n<li>Science Core Technology Programme</li>\n<li>General Study Programme</li>\n<li>European Component Initiative</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Optional">Optional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Optional">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Depending on their individual choices the countries can contribute to the following programmes, listed according to:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Launchers</li>\n<li>Earth Observation</li>\n<li>Human Spaceflight and Exploration</li>\n<li>Telecommunications</li>\n<li>Navigation</li>\n<li>Space Situational Awareness</li>\n<li>Technology</li></ul>\n<h2><span id="Member_states.2C_funding_and_budget"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states,_funding_and_budget">Member states, funding and budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Member states, funding and budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_and_contribution_to_ESA">Membership and contribution to ESA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Membership and contribution to ESA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #5FB4A1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ECS states</div></abbr><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3D9345; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Signatories of the Cooperation Agreement</div></div></div></div></div>\n<p>By 2015, ESA was an intergovernmental organisation of 22 member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-members-6">[6]</a></sup> Member states participate to varying degrees in the mandatory (25% of total expenditures in 2008) and optional space programmes (75% of total expenditures in 2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-czechspace.cz_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-czechspace.cz-17">[17]</a></sup> The 2008 budget amounted to &#8364;3.0 billion the 2009 budget to &#8364;3.6 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The total budget amounted to about &#8364;3.7 billion in 2010, &#8364;3.99 billion in 2011, &#8364;4.02 billion in 2012, &#8364;4.28 billion in 2013, &#8364;4.10 billion in 2014 and &#8364;4.33 billion in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budget2013_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-budget2013-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_budget_for_2011_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESA_budget_for_2011-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_budget_for_2012_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESA_budget_for_2012-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budget2014_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-budget2014-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budget2015_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-budget2015-23">[23]</a></sup> Languages generally used are English and French. Additionally, official documents are also provided in German and documents regarding the <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">Spacelab</a> are also provided in Italian. If found appropriate, the agency may conduct its correspondence in any language of a member state.\n</p><p>The following table lists all the member states and adjunct members, their ESA convention ratification dates, and their contributions in 2019:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budget2019_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-budget2019-3">[3]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table cellspacing="2" class="wikitable id="Non-full_member_states">Non-full member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Non-full member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Currently the only associated member state is Slovenia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa.int2_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-esa.int2-39">[35]</a></sup> Previously associated members were Austria, Norway and Finland, all of which later joined ESA as full members.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Since 1 January 1979, Canada has had the special status of a Cooperating State within ESA. By virtue of this accord, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">Canadian Space Agency</a> takes part in ESA\'s deliberative bodies and decision-making and also in ESA\'s programmes and activities. Canadian firms can bid for and receive contracts to work on programmes. The accord has a provision ensuring a fair industrial return to Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[37]</a></sup> The most recent Cooperation Agreement was signed on 2010-12-15 with a term extending to 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[39]</a></sup> For 2014, Canada\'s annual assessed contribution to the ESA general budget was &#8364;6,059,449 (<a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">CAD$</a>8,559,050).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[40]</a></sup> For 2017, Canada has increased its annual contribution to &#8364;21,600,000 (<a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">CAD$</a>30,000,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[41]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget_appropriation_and_allocation">Budget appropriation and allocation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Budget appropriation and allocation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:482px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Easbars.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="1088" decoding="async" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Easbars.png/480px-Easbars.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Easbars.png/720px-Easbars.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Easbars.png/960px-Easbars.png 2x" width="480"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Easbars.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>European Space Agency 2016 budget by domain out of a total budget is 5250M&#8364;.</div></div></div>\n<p>ESA is funded from annual contributions by <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">national</a> governments as well as from an annual contribution by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sn20150727_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-sn20150727-47">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The budget of ESA was &#8364;5.250 billion in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa2016budpie_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-esa2016budpie-48">[43]</a></sup> Every 3&#8211;4 years, ESA member states agree on a budget plan for several years at an ESA member states conference. This plan can be amended in future years, however provides the major guideline for ESA for several years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The 2016 budget allocations for major areas of ESA activity are shown in the chart on the right.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa2016budpie_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-esa2016budpie-48">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Countries typically have their own space programmes that differ in how they operate organisationally and financially with ESA. For example, the French space agency CNES has a total budget of &#8364;2015 million, of which &#8364;755 million is paid as direct financial contribution to ESA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leCNES_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-leCNES-49">[44]</a></sup> Several space-related projects are joint projects between national space agencies and ESA (e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/COROT" title="COROT">COROT</a>). Also, ESA is not the only European governmental space organisation (for example <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Satellite_Centre" title="European Union Satellite Centre">European Union Satellite Centre</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlargement">Enlargement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Enlargement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Space_Agency" title="Enlargement of the European Space Agency">Enlargement of the European Space Agency</a></div>\n<p>After the decision of the ESA Council of 21/22 March 2001, the procedure for accession of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_states" title="European states">European states</a> was detailed as described the document titled "The Plan for European Co-operating States (PECS)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[45]</a></sup>\nNations that want to become a full member of ESA do so in 3 stages. First a Cooperation Agreement is signed between the country and ESA. In this stage, the country has very limited financial responsibilities. If a country wants to co-operate more fully with ESA, it signs a European Cooperating State (ECS) Agreement. The ECS Agreement makes companies based in the country eligible for participation in ESA procurements. The country can also participate in all ESA programmes, except for the Basic Technology Research Programme. While the financial contribution of the country concerned increases, it is still much lower than that of a full member state. The agreement is normally followed by a Plan For European Cooperating State (or PECS Charter). This is a 5-year programme of basic research and development activities aimed at improving the nation\'s space industry capacity. At the end of the 5-year period, the country can either begin negotiations to become a full member state or an associated state or sign a new PECS Charter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[46]</a></sup> Many countries, most of which joined the EU in both 2004 and 2007, have started to co-operate with ESA on various levels:\n</p>\n<table cellspacing="2" class="unsortable">National Programme\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="15" href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-70">[65]</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[67]</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Space_Research_and_Technology_Institute" title="Space Research and Technology Institute">SRTI</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="12" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>\n</td>\n<td>2013\n</td>\n<td>19 February 2018<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[68]</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>through <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Science_and_Education_(Croatia)" title="Ministry of Science and Education (Croatia)">MoSE</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>During the Ministerial Meeting in December 2014, ESA ministers approved a resolution calling for discussions to begin with Israel, Australia and South Africa on future association agreements. The ministers noted that &#8220;concrete cooperation is at an advanced stage&#8221; with these nations and that &#8220;prospects for mutual benefits are existing&#8221;.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parabolicarc.com_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-parabolicarc.com-74">[69]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A separate space exploration strategy resolution calls for further co-operation with the United States, Russia and China on "LEO exploration, including a continuation of ISS cooperation and the development of a robust plan for the coordinated use of space transportation vehicles and systems for exploration purposes, participation in robotic missions for the exploration of the Moon, the robotic exploration of Mars, leading to a broad Mars Sample Return mission in which Europe should be involved as a full partner, and human missions beyond LEO in the longer term."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parabolicarc.com_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-parabolicarc.com-74">[69]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EU_and_the_European_Space_Agency">EU and the European Space Agency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: EU and the European Space Agency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The political perspective of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) was to make ESA an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agency_of_the_European_Union" title="Agency of the European Union">agency of the EU</a> by 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[70]</a></sup> although this date was not met. The EU is already the largest single donor to ESA\'s budget and non-ESA EU states are observers at ESA.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_vehicle_fleet">Launch vehicle fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Launch vehicle fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>ESA has a fleet of different launch vehicles in service with which it competes in all sectors of the launch market. ESA\'s fleet consists of three major rocket designs: <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz-2_(rocket)" title="Soyuz-2 (rocket)">Soyuz-2</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vega_(launcher)" title="Vega (launcher)">Vega</a>. Rocket launches are carried out by <a href="/wiki/Arianespace" title="Arianespace">Arianespace</a>, which has 23 shareholders representing the industry that manufactures the Ariane 5 as well as <a href="/wiki/CNES" title="CNES">CNES</a>, at ESA\'s <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">Guiana Space Centre</a>. Because many communication satellites have equatorial orbits, launches from French Guiana are able to take larger payloads into space than from spaceports at higher <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a>. In addition, equatorial launches give spacecraft an extra \'push\' of nearly 500&#160;m/s due to the higher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotational_velocity" title="Rotational velocity">rotational velocity</a> of the Earth at the equator compared to near the Earth\'s poles where rotational velocity approaches zero.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ariane_5">Ariane 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ariane 5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2419" data-file-width="3226" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg/220px-Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg/330px-Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg/440px-Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ariane_5ECA_on_its_way_to_launch_pad_ELA-3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a> ECA transported to the <a href="/wiki/ELA-3" title="ELA-3">ELA-3</a> launch pad</div></div></div>\n<p>The Ariane 5 rocket is ESA\'s primary launcher. It has been in service since 1997 and replaced <a href="/wiki/Ariane_4" title="Ariane 4">Ariane 4</a>. Two different <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5#Variants" title="Ariane 5">variants</a> are currently in use. The heaviest and most used version, the <span class="nowrap">Ariane 5 ECA</span>, delivers two communications satellites of up to 10 tonnes into <a href="/wiki/Geostationary_transfer_orbit" title="Geostationary transfer orbit">GTO</a>. It failed during its first test flight in 2002, but has since made 82 consecutive successful <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5#Ariane_5_flights" title="Ariane 5">flights</a> until a partial failure in January 2018. The other version, <span class="nowrap">Ariane 5 ES</span>, was used to launch the <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">Automated Transfer Vehicle</a> (ATV) to the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> (ISS) and will be used to launch four <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a> navigational satellites at a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2012, ESA agreed to build an upgraded variant called <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5#Ariane_5_ME" title="Ariane 5"><span class="nowrap">Ariane 5 ME</span></a> (Mid-life Evolution) which would increase payload capacity to 11.5 tonnes to GTO and feature a restartable second stage to allow more complex missions. Ariane 5 ME was scheduled to fly in 2018<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[73]</a></sup>, but the whole project was scrapped in favor of <a href="/wiki/Ariane_6" title="Ariane 6">Ariane 6</a>, planned to replace Ariane 5 in the 2020s.\n</p><p>ESA\'s <a href="/wiki/Ariane_1" title="Ariane 1">Ariane 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ariane_2" title="Ariane 2">2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ariane_3" title="Ariane 3">3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ariane_4" title="Ariane 4">4</a> launchers (the last of which was ESA\'s long-time workhorse) have been retired.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soyuz">Soyuz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Soyuz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_at_the_Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Soyuz at the Guiana Space Centre">Soyuz at the Guiana Space Centre</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG/220px-CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG/330px-CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG/440px-CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CSG_Soyuz_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ensemble_de_Lancement_Soyouz" title="Ensemble de Lancement Soyouz">Soyuz Launch Complex</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz-2_(rocket)" title="Soyuz-2 (rocket)">Soyuz-2</a> (also called the Soyuz-ST or Soyuz-STK) is a Russian medium <a href="/wiki/Payload" title="Payload">payload</a> launcher (ca. 3 metric tons to <a href="/wiki/Geostationary_transfer_orbit" title="Geostationary transfer orbit">GTO</a>) which was brought into ESA service in October 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VS01_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-VS01-79">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[75]</a></sup> ESA entered into a &#8364;340 million joint venture with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">Russian Federal Space Agency</a> over the use of the Soyuz launcher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-international-coop_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-international-coop-11">[11]</a></sup> Under the agreement, the Russian agency manufactures Soyuz rocket parts for ESA, which are then shipped to French Guiana for assembly.\n</p><p>ESA benefits because it gains a medium payload launcher, complementing its fleet while saving on development costs. In addition, the Soyuz rocket&#8212;which has been the Russian\'s space launch workhorse for some 40 years&#8212;is proven technology with a very good safety record. Russia benefits in that it gets access to the Kourou launch site. Due to its proximity to the equator, launching from Kourou rather than <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">Baikonur</a> nearly doubles Soyuz\'s payload to <a href="/wiki/Geostationary_transfer_orbit" title="Geostationary transfer orbit">GTO</a> (3.0 tonnes vs. 1.7 tonnes).\n</p><p>Soyuz first launched from Kourou on 21 October 2011, and successfully placed two <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a> satellites into orbit 23,222 kilometres above Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VS01_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-VS01-79">[74]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vega">Vega</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Vega">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1001" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg/220px-Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg/330px-Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg/440px-Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sentinel-2_and_vega.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vega rocket</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vega_(rocket)" title="Vega (rocket)">Vega (rocket)</a></div>\n<p>Vega is ESA\'s carrier for small satellites. Developed by seven ESA members led by <a href="/wiki/Italian_Space_Agency" title="Italian Space Agency">Italy</a>, it is capable of carrying a payload with a mass of between 300 and 1500&#160;kg to an altitude of 700&#160;km, for low <a href="/wiki/Polar_orbit" title="Polar orbit">polar orbit</a>. Its maiden launch from <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">Kourou</a> was on 13 February 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[76]</a></sup> Vega began full commercial exploitation in December 2015 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rocket has three solid propulsion stages and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_rocket" title="Liquid rocket">liquid propulsion</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_stage" title="Upper stage">upper stage</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AVUM" title="AVUM">AVUM</a>) for accurate orbital insertion and the ability to place multiple <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" title="Payload (air and space craft)">payloads</a> into different orbits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ariane_launch_vehicle_development_funding">Ariane launch vehicle development funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ariane launch vehicle development funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Historically, the Ariane family rockets have been funded primarily "with money contributed by ESA governments seeking to participate in the program rather than through competitive industry bids. This [has meant that] governments commit multiyear funding to the development with the expectation of a roughly 90% return on investment in the form of industrial workshare."  ESA is proposing changes to this scheme by moving to <a href="/wiki/Competition_(economics)" title="Competition (economics)">competitive</a> bids for the development of the <a href="/wiki/Ariane_6" title="Ariane 6">Ariane 6</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aw20140310_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-aw20140310-85">[80]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_space_flight">Human space flight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Human space flight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="475" decoding="async" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg/170px-Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg/255px-Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg/340px-Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ulf_D._Merbold.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ulf_Merbold" title="Ulf Merbold">Ulf Merbold</a> became the first ESA astronaut to fly into space.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the time ESA was formed, its main goals did not encompass human space flight; rather it considered itself to be primarily a scientific research organisation for unmanned space exploration in contrast to its American and Soviet counterparts. It is therefore not surprising that the first non-Soviet European in space was not an ESA astronaut on a European space craft; it was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czechoslovak" title="Czechoslovak">Czechoslovak</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladim%C3%ADr_Remek" title="Vladim&#237;r Remek">Vladim&#237;r Remek</a> who in 1978 became the first non-Soviet or American in space (the first man in space being <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> of the Soviet Union) &#8211; on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_space_programme" title="Soviet space programme">Soviet</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">Soyuz spacecraft</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Pole</a> <a href="/wiki/Miros%C5%82aw_Hermaszewski" title="Miros&#322;aw Hermaszewski">Miros&#322;aw Hermaszewski</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_German" title="East German">East German</a> <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_J%C3%A4hn" title="Sigmund J&#228;hn">Sigmund J&#228;hn</a> in the same year. This Soviet co-operation programme, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercosmos" title="Intercosmos">Intercosmos</a>, primarily involved the participation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_bloc" title="Eastern bloc">Eastern bloc</a> countries. In 1982, however, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Loup_Chr%C3%A9tien" title="Jean-Loup Chr&#233;tien">Jean-Loup Chr&#233;tien</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/Western_Bloc" title="Western Bloc">non-Communist Bloc</a> astronaut on a flight to the Soviet <a href="/wiki/Salyut_7" title="Salyut 7">Salyut 7</a> space station.\n</p><p>Because Chr&#233;tien did not officially fly into space as an ESA astronaut, but rather as a member of the French <a href="/wiki/CNES" title="CNES">CNES</a> astronaut corps, the German <a href="/wiki/Ulf_Merbold" title="Ulf Merbold">Ulf Merbold</a> is considered the first ESA astronaut to fly into space. He participated in the <a href="/wiki/STS-9" title="STS-9">STS-9</a> <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> mission that included the first use of the European-built <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">Spacelab</a> in 1983. STS-9 marked the beginning of an extensive ESA/NASA joint partnership that included dozens of space flights of ESA astronauts in the following years. Some of these missions with Spacelab were fully funded and organizationally and scientifically controlled by ESA (such as two missions by Germany and one by Japan) with European astronauts as full crew members rather than guests on board. Beside paying for Spacelab flights and seats on the shuttles, ESA continued its human space flight co-operation with the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and later Russia, including numerous visits to <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>.\n</p><p>During the latter half of the 1980s, European human space flights changed from being the exception to routine and therefore, in 1990, the <a href="/wiki/European_Astronaut_Centre" title="European Astronaut Centre">European Astronaut Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, Germany was established. It selects and trains prospective astronauts and is responsible for the co-ordination with international partners, especially with regard to the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. As of 2006, the ESA astronaut corps officially included twelve members, including nationals from most large European countries except the United Kingdom.\n</p><p>In the summer of 2008, ESA started to recruit new astronauts so that final selection would be due in spring 2009. Almost 10,000 people registered as astronaut candidates before registration ended in June 2008. 8,413 fulfilled the initial application criteria. Of the applicants, 918 were chosen to take part in the first stage of psychological testing, which narrowed down the field to 192. After two-stage psychological tests and medical evaluation in early 2009, as well as formal interviews, six new members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Astronaut_Corps" title="European Astronaut Corps">European Astronaut Corps</a> were selected - five men and one woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Astronaut_names">Astronaut names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Astronaut names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/European_Astronaut_Corps" title="European Astronaut Corps">European Astronaut Corps</a></div>\n<p>The astronauts of the European Space Agency are:\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns 1]</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><img alt="Italy" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="15" Vittori</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS_89-14"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-89">[note 3]</a></sup></li></ul>\n</div>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Mir-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Mir_87-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mir_87-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mir_87-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mir_87-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Mir_87-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">have visited <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-selection2009-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-selection2009_88-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a selection</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-ISS-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-ISS_89-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a
