href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-retired-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-retired_90-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-retired_90-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-retired_90-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-retired_90-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-retired_90-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">now retired</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crew_vehicles">Crew vehicles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Crew vehicles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the 1980s, France pressed for an independent European crew launch vehicle. Around 1978 it was decided to pursue a reusable spacecraft model and starting in November 1987 a project to create a mini-shuttle by the name of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hermes_(shuttle)" title="Hermes (shuttle)">Hermes</a> was introduced. The craft was comparable to early proposals for the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> and consisted of a small reusable spaceship that would carry 3 to 5 astronauts and 3 to 4 metric tons of payload for scientific experiments. With a total maximum weight of 21 metric tons it would have been launched on the <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">Ariane 5</a> rocket, which was being developed at that time. It was planned solely for use in <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> space flights. The planning and pre-development phase concluded in 1991; the production phase was never fully implemented because at that time the political landscape had changed significantly. With the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> ESA looked forward to co-operation with Russia to build a next-generation space vehicle. Thus the Hermes programme was cancelled in 1995 after about 3 billion dollars had been spent. The <a href="/wiki/Columbus_Man-Tended_Free_Flyer" title="Columbus Man-Tended Free Flyer">Columbus space station programme</a> had a similar fate.\n</p><p>In the 21st century, ESA started new programmes in order to create its own crew vehicles, most notable among its various projects and proposals is <a href="/wiki/Hopper_(spacecraft)" title="Hopper (spacecraft)">Hopper</a>, whose prototype by <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">EADS</a>, called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EADS_Phoenix" title="EADS Phoenix">Phoenix</a>, has already been tested. While projects such as <a href="/wiki/Hopper_(spacecraft)" title="Hopper (spacecraft)">Hopper</a> are neither concrete nor to be realised within the next decade, other possibilities for human spaceflight in co-operation with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Space_Agency" title="Russian Space Agency">Russian Space Agency</a> have emerged. Following talks with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Space_Agency" title="Russian Space Agency">Russian Space Agency</a> in 2004 and June 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[86]</a></sup> a co-operation between ESA and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Space_Agency" title="Russian Space Agency">Russian Space Agency</a> was announced to jointly work on the Russian-designed <a href="/wiki/Kliper" title="Kliper">Kliper</a>, a reusable spacecraft that would be available for space travel beyond LEO (e.g. the moon or even Mars). It was speculated that Europe would finance part of it. A &#8364;50 million participation study for Kliper, which was expected to be approved in December 2005, was finally not approved by the ESA member states. The Russian state tender for the project was subsequently cancelled in 2006.\n</p><p>In June 2006, ESA member states granted 15 million to the <a href="/wiki/CSTS" title="CSTS">Crew Space Transportation System</a> (CSTS) study, a two-year study to design a spacecraft capable of going beyond Low-Earth orbit based on the current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">Soyuz</a> design. This project was pursued with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roskosmos" title="Roskosmos">Roskosmos</a> instead of the cancelled Kliper proposal. A decision on the actual implementation and construction of the CSTS spacecraft was contemplated for 2008.\nIn mid-2009 EADS Astrium was awarded a &#8364;21 million study into designing a crew vehicle based on the European ATV which is believed to now be the basis of the Advanced Crew Transportation System design.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[87]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2012, ESA decided to join NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">Orion programme</a>. The ATV would form the basis of a propulsion unit for NASA\'s new manned spacecraft. ESA may also seek to work with NASA on Orion\'s launch system as well in order to secure a seat on the spacecraft for its own astronauts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2014, ESA signed an agreement with <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_Corporation" title="Sierra Nevada Corporation">Sierra Nevada Corporation</a> for co-operation in <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chaser" title="Dream Chaser">Dream Chaser</a> project. Further studies on the Dream Chaser for European Utilization or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DC4EU" title="DC4EU">DC4EU</a> project were funded, including the feasibility of launching a Europeanized Dream Chaser onboard Ariane 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA_signs_agreement_2014_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESA_signs_agreement_2014-98">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBDM_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBDM-99">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_with_other_countries_and_organisations">Cooperation with other countries and organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cooperation with other countries and organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>ESA has signed co-operation agreements with the following states that currently neither plan to integrate as tightly with ESA institutions as Canada, nor envision future membership of ESA: Argentina,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[91]</a></sup> Brazil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[92]</a></sup> China,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[93]</a></sup> India<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[94]</a></sup> (for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chandrayan" title="Chandrayan">Chandrayan</a> mission), Russia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AR2003_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-AR2003-104">[95]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[96]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Additionally, ESA has joint projects with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> of the United States and is participating in the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> together with the United States (NASA), Russia and Japan (JAXA).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ESA_and_EU.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ESA_and_EU.png/220px-ESA_and_EU.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ESA_and_EU.png/330px-ESA_and_EU.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ESA_and_EU.png/440px-ESA_and_EU.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ESA_and_EU.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #81c846; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ESA and EU member states</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b94954; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;ESA-only members</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3b54b1; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU-only members</div></div></div></div>\n<p>ESA is not an agency or body of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), and has non-EU countries (Norway, and Switzerland) as members. There are however ties between the two, with various agreements in place and being worked on, to define the legal status of ESA with regard to the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dqbiya_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-dqbiya-106">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are common goals between ESA and the EU. ESA has an EU liaison office in Brussels. On certain projects, the EU and ESA co-operate, such as the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo</a> satellite navigation system. Space policy has since December 2009 been an area for voting in the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>. Under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Space_Policy" title="European Space Policy">European Space Policy of 2007</a>, the EU, ESA and its Member States committed themselves to increasing co-ordination of their activities and programmes and to organising their respective roles relating to space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Lisbon Treaty of 2009 reinforces the case for space in Europe and strengthens the role of ESA as an R&amp;D space agency. Article 189 of the Treaty gives the EU a mandate to elaborate a European space policy and take related measures, and provides that the EU should establish appropriate relations with ESA.\n</p><p>Former Italian astronaut <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Guidoni" title="Umberto Guidoni">Umberto Guidoni</a>, during his tenure as a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Member of the European Parliament</a> from 2004 to 2009, stressed the importance of the European Union as a driving force for space exploration, "since other players are coming up such as India and China it is becoming ever more important that Europeans can have an independent access to space. We have to invest more into space research and technology in order to have an industry capable of competing with other international players."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first EU-ESA International Conference on Human Space Exploration took place in Prague on 22 and 23 October 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[100]</a></sup> A road map which would lead to a common vision and strategic planning in the area of space exploration was discussed. Ministers from all 29 EU and ESA members as well as members of parliament were in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[101]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_space_organisations_of_member_states">National space organisations of member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: National space organisations of member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>The <i><a href="/wiki/CNES" title="CNES">Centre National d\'&#201;tudes Spatiales</a></i> (CNES) (National Centre for Space Study) is the French government space agency (administratively, a "public establishment of industrial and commercial character"). Its headquarters are in central <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. CNES is the main participant on the Ariane project. Indeed, CNES designed and tested all Ariane family rockets (mainly from its centre in <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vry,_Essonne" title="&#201;vry, Essonne">&#201;vry</a> near <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>)</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/UK_Space_Agency" title="UK Space Agency">UK Space Agency</a> is a partnership of the UK government departments which are active in space. Through the UK Space Agency, the partners provide delegates to represent the UK on the various ESA governing bodies. Each partner funds its own programme.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Italian_Space_Agency" title="Italian Space Agency">Italian Space Agency</a> (<i>Agenzia Spaziale Italiana</i> or ASI) was founded in 1988 to promote, co-ordinate and conduct space activities in Italy. Operating under the Ministry of the Universities and of Scientific and Technological Research, the agency cooperates with numerous entities active in space technology and with the president of the Council of Ministers. Internationally, the ASI provides Italy\'s delegation to the Council of the European Space Agency and to its subordinate bodies.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/German_Aerospace_Center" title="German Aerospace Center">German Aerospace Center</a> (DLR) (German: <i>Deutsches Zentrum f&#252;r Luft- und Raumfahrt e. V.</i>) is the national research centre for aviation and space flight of the Federal Republic of Germany and of other member states in the <a href="/wiki/Helmholtz_Association_of_German_Research_Centres" title="Helmholtz Association of German Research Centres">Helmholtz Association</a>. Its extensive research and development projects are included in national and international cooperative programmes. In addition to its research projects, the centre is the assigned space agency of Germany bestowing headquarters of German space flight activities and its associates.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Nacional_de_T%C3%A9cnica_Aeroespacial" title="Instituto Nacional de T&#233;cnica Aeroespacial">Instituto Nacional de T&#233;cnica Aeroespacial</a> (INTA) (National Institute for Aerospace Technique) is a Public Research Organization specialised in aerospace research and technology development in Spain. Among other functions, it serves as a platform for space research and acts as a significant testing facility for the aeronautic and space sector in the country.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NASA">NASA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: NASA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>ESA has a long history of collaboration with <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>. Since ESA\'s astronaut corps was formed, the <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> has been the primary launch vehicle used by ESA\'s astronauts to get into space through partnership programmes with NASA. In the 1980s and 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Spacelab" title="Spacelab">Spacelab</a> programme was an ESA-NASA joint research programme that had ESA develop and manufacture orbital labs for the Space Shuttle for several flights on which ESA participate with astronauts in experiments.\n</p><p>In robotic science mission and exploration missions, NASA has been ESA\'s main partner. <i><a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini&#8211;Huygens">Cassini&#8211;Huygens</a></i> was a joint NASA-ESA mission, along with the <a href="/wiki/Infrared_Space_Observatory" title="Infrared Space Observatory">Infrared Space Observatory</a>, <a href="/wiki/INTEGRAL" title="INTEGRAL">INTEGRAL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_and_Heliospheric_Observatory" title="Solar and Heliospheric Observatory">SOHO</a>, and others. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">Hubble Space Telescope</a> is a joint project of NASA and ESA. Future ESA-NASA joint projects include the <a href="/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope" title="James Webb Space Telescope">James Webb Space Telescope</a> and the proposed <a href="/wiki/Laser_Interferometer_Space_Antenna" title="Laser Interferometer Space Antenna">Laser Interferometer Space Antenna</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> NASA has committed to provide support to ESA\'s proposed <a class="external text" href="http://us-marcopolor.jhuapl.edu/" rel="nofollow">MarcoPolo-R</a> mission to return an asteroid sample to Earth for further analysis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> NASA and ESA will also likely join together for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Sample_Return_Mission" title="Mars Sample Return Mission">Mars Sample Return Mission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[102]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_with_other_space_agencies">Cooperation with other space agencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cooperation with other space agencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since China has started to invest more money into space activities, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Space_Agency" title="Chinese Space Agency">Chinese Space Agency</a> has sought international partnerships. ESA is, beside the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Space_Agency" title="Russian Space Agency">Russian Space Agency</a>, one of its most important partners. Two space agencies cooperated in the development of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double_Star_Mission" title="Double Star Mission">Double Star Mission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[103]</a></sup> In 2017, ESA sent two astronauts to China for two weeks sea survival training with Chinese astronauts in <a href="/wiki/Yantai" title="Yantai">Yantai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shandong" title="Shandong">Shandong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[104]</a></sup>\n</p><p>ESA entered into a major joint venture with Russia in the form of the <a href="/wiki/CSTS" title="CSTS">CSTS</a>, the preparation of <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> spaceport for launches of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz-2_(rocket)" title="Soyuz-2 (rocket)">Soyuz-2</a> rockets and other projects. With India, ESA agreed to send instruments into space aboard the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISRO" title="ISRO">ISRO</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-1" title="Chandrayaan-1">Chandrayaan-1</a> in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[105]</a></sup> ESA is also co-operating with Japan, the most notable current project in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">JAXA</a> is the <i><a href="/wiki/BepiColombo" title="BepiColombo">BepiColombo</a></i> mission to <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>.\n</p><p>Speaking to reporters at an air show near Moscow in August 2011, ESA head Jean-Jacques Dordain said ESA and Russia\'s Roskosmos space agency would "carry out the first flight to Mars together."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Space_Station">International Space Station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: International Space Station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/European_contribution_to_the_International_Space_Station" title="European contribution to the International Space Station">European contribution to the International Space Station</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="912" data-file-width="1168" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg/220px-Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg/330px-Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg/440px-Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbus_module_delivered_to_KSC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Columbus_(ISS_module)" title="Columbus (ISS module)">ISS module Columbus</a></i> at Kennedy Space Center\'s <a href="/wiki/Space_Station_Processing_Facility" title="Space Station Processing Facility">Space Station Processing Facility</a></div></div></div>\n<p>With regard to the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> (ISS) ESA is not represented by all of its member states:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[107]</a></sup> 10 of the 21 ESA member states currently participate in the project: Belgium, Denmark, France, Germany, Italy, Netherlands, Norway, Spain, Sweden and Switzerland. Austria, Finland and Ireland chose not to participate, because of lack of interest or concerns about the expense of the project. The United Kingdom withdrew from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Space_Station_programme" title="International Space Station programme">preliminary agreement</a> because of concerns about the expense of the project. Portugal, Luxembourg, Greece, the Czech Republic, Romania and Poland joined ESA after the agreement had been signed. ESA is taking part in the construction and operation of the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a> with contributions such as <a href="/wiki/Columbus_(ISS_module)" title="Columbus (ISS module)">Columbus</a>, a science laboratory module that was brought into orbit by NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/STS-122" title="STS-122">STS-122</a> <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">Space Shuttle</a> mission and the <a href="/wiki/Cupola_(ISS_module)" title="Cupola (ISS module)">Cupola</a> observatory module that was completed in July 2005 by <a href="/wiki/Alenia_Aeronautica" title="Alenia Aeronautica">Alenia Spazio</a> for ESA. The current estimates for the ISS are approaching &#8364;100 billion in total (development, construction and 10 years of maintaining the station) of which ESA has committed to paying &#8364;8 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[108]</a></sup> About 90% of the costs of ESA\'s ISS share will be contributed by Germany (41%), France (28%) and Italy (20%). German ESA astronaut <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Reiter" title="Thomas Reiter">Thomas Reiter</a> was the first long-term ISS crew member.\n</p><p>ESA has developed the <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">Automated Transfer Vehicle</a> for ISS resupply. Each ATV has a cargo capacity of 7,667 kilograms (16,903&#160;lb).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atvspecs_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-atvspecs-118">[109]</a></sup> The first ATV, <i><a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne_ATV" title="Jules Verne ATV">Jules Verne</a></i>, was launched on 9 March 2008 and on 3 April 2008 successfully docked with the ISS. This manoeuvre, considered a major technical feat, involved using automated systems to allow the ATV to track the ISS, moving at 27,000&#160;km/h, and attach itself with an accuracy of 2&#160;cm.\n</p><p>As of 2013, the spacecraft establishing supply links to the ISS are the Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_spacecraft" title="Progress spacecraft">Progress</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">Soyuz</a>, European <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">ATV</a>, Japanese <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">Kounotori (HTV)</a>, and the USA <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">COTS</a> program vehicles <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">Dragon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_(spacecraft)" title="Cygnus (spacecraft)">Cygnus</a>.\n</p><p>European Life and Physical Sciences research on board the International Space Station (ISS) is mainly based on the <a href="/wiki/European_Programme_for_Life_and_Physical_Sciences_in_Space" title="European Programme for Life and Physical Sciences in Space">European Programme for Life and Physical Sciences in Space</a> programme that was initiated in 2001.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to Annex 1, Resolution No. 8 of the <i>ESA Convention and Council Rules of Procedure</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Space_Agency_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-European_Space_Agency-4">[4]</a></sup> English, French and German may be used in all meetings of the Agency, with interpretation provided into these three languages. All official documents are available in English and French with all documents concerning the ESA Council being available in German as well.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_(12052189474).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_%2812052189474%29.jpg/220px-Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_%2812052189474%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_%2812052189474%29.jpg/330px-Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_%2812052189474%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_%2812052189474%29.jpg/440px-Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_%2812052189474%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Views_in_the_Main_Control_Room_(12052189474).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ESA Mission Control at <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Operations_Centre" title="European Space Operations Centre">ESOC</a> in <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a>, Germany</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>ESA Headquarters (HQ), <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Space_Operations_Centre" title="European Space Operations Centre">European Space Operations Centre</a> (ESOC), <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Space_Research_and_Technology_Centre" title="European Space Research and Technology Centre">European Space Research and Technology Centre</a> (ESTEC), <a href="/wiki/Noordwijk" title="Noordwijk">Noordwijk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">The Netherlands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Space_Astronomy_Centre" title="European Space Astronomy Centre">European Space Astronomy Centre</a> (ESAC), <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[110]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Centre_for_Space_Applications_and_Telecommunications" title="European Centre for Space Applications and Telecommunications">European Centre for Space Applications and Telecommunications</a> (ECSAT), <a href="/wiki/Oxfordshire" title="Oxfordshire">Oxfordshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[111]</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Astronaut_Centre" title="European Astronaut Centre">European Astronaut Centre</a> (EAC), <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, Germany</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/ESA_Centre_for_Earth_Observation" title="ESA Centre for Earth Observation">ESA Centre for Earth Observation</a> (ESRIN), <a href="/wiki/Frascati" title="Frascati">Frascati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_Spatial_Guyanais" title="Centre Spatial Guyanais">Guiana Space Centre</a> (CSG), <a href="/wiki/Kourou" title="Kourou">Kourou</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/ESTRACK" title="ESTRACK">European Space Tracking Network</a> (ESTRACK)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Data_Relay_System" title="European Data Relay System">European Data Relay System</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="ESA_and_the_EU_institutions">ESA and the EU institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: ESA and the EU institutions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">Flag of Europe</a> is the one to be flown in space during missions (for example it was flown by ESA\'s Andre Kuipers during Delta mission)\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">Commission</a> is increasingly working together towards common objectives. Some 20 per cent of the funds managed by ESA now originate from the supranational <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">budget of the European Union</a>.\n</p><p>However, in recent years the ties between ESA and the European institutions have been reinforced by the increasing role that space plays in supporting Europe&#8217;s social, political and economic policies.\n</p><p>The legal basis for the EU/ESA co-operation is provided by a Framework Agreement which entered into force in May 2004. According to this agreement, the European Commission and ESA co-ordinate their actions through the Joint Secretariat, a small team of EC&#8217;s administrators and ESA executive. The Member States of the two organisations meet at ministerial level in the Space Council, which is a concomitant meeting of the EU and ESA Councils, prepared by Member States representatives in the High-level Space Policy Group (HSPG).\n</p><p>ESA maintains a liaison office in Brussels to facilitate relations with the European institutions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guaranteeing_European_access_to_space">Guaranteeing European access to space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Guaranteeing European access to space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In May 2007, the 29 European countries expressed their support for the European Space Policy in a resolution of the Space Council, unifying the approach of ESA with those of the European Union and their member states.\n</p><p>Prepared jointly by the European Commission and ESA&#8217;s Director General, the European Space Policy sets out a basic vision and strategy for the space sector and addresses issues such as security and defence, access to space and exploration.\n</p><p>Through this resolution, the EU, ESA and their Member States all commit to increasing co-ordination of their activities and programmes and their respective roles relating to space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[112]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_Space_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 3 August 1984, the ESA\'s <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> headquarters were severely damaged and six people were hurt when a bomb exploded, planted by the far-left armed <a href="/wiki/Action_directe_(armed_group)" title="Action directe (armed group)">Action Directe</a> group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[113]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 December 2015, hackers from <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_(group)" title="Anonymous (group)">Anonymous</a> breached the ESA\'s subdomains and leaked thousands of login credentials.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span integration#Space</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Launcher_Development_Organisation" title="European Launcher Development Organisation">European Launcher Development Organisation</a> (ELDO)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Space_Research_Organisation" title="European Space Research Organisation">European Space Research Organisation</a> (ESRO)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eurospace" Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 March</span> 2014</span>. <q><i>ESA Director General Jean-Jacques Dordain is aiming to reduce the agency\'s development and operational costs in a stark departure from past practice: Until now, the Ariane family of rockets has been built largely with money contributed by ESA governments seeking to participate in the program rather than through competitive industry bids. This means governments commit multiyear funding to the development with the expectation of a roughly 90% return on investment in the form of industrial workshare.  But in July, when Dordain presents ESA\'s member states with industry proposals for building the Ariane 6, he will seek government contributions based on the best value for money, not geographic return on investment. \'To have competitive launchers, we need to rethink the launch sector in Europe.\'</i></q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Aviation+Week&amp;rft.atitle=SpaceX+Says+Falcon+9+To+Compete+For+EELV+This+Year&amp;rft.date=2014-03-10&amp;rft.aulast=Svitak&amp;rft.aufirst=Amy&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.aviationweek.com%2FArticle.aspx%3Fid%3D%2Farticle-xml%2FAW_03_10_2014_p48-668592.xml&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEuropean+Space+Agency"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.esa.int/Our_Activities/Human_Spaceflight/Closing_in_on_new_astronauts" rel="nofollow">"Closing in on new astronauts"</a>.
